       <tr>
        <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Morocco.svg">

       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
          <ul>
           <li class="nv-view">
            <a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Morocco" title="Template:History of Morocco">
             <abbr title="View this template">
              v
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-talk">
            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Morocco" title="Template talk:History of Morocco">
             <abbr title="Discuss this template">
              t
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-edit">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit">
             <abbr title="Edit this template">
              e
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        history of
        <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
         Morocco
        </a>
       </b>
       spans several millennia, succeeding the prehistoric cultures of
       <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Irhoud" title="Jebel Irhoud">
        Jebel Irhoud
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Taforalt" title="Taforalt">
        Taforalt
       </a>
       . It dates from the establishment of
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">
        Mauretania
       </a>
       and other ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">
        Berber
       </a>
       kingdoms, to the establishment of the Moroccan state by the
       <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">
        Idrisid dynasty
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       followed by other Islamic dynasties, through to the colonial and independence periods.
      </p>
      <p>
       Archaeological evidence has shown that the area was inhabited by
       <a href="/wiki/Hominidae" title="Hominidae">
        hominids
       </a>
       at least 400,000 years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hublin_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hublin-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The recorded history of
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       begins with the
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenician
       </a>
       colonization of the Moroccan coast between the 8th and 6th centuries BC,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pe5_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pe5-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although the area was inhabited by
       <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">
        indigenous Berbers
       </a>
       for some two thousand years before that. In the 5th century BC, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">
        city-state of Carthage
       </a>
       extended its hegemony over the coastal areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pe7-9_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pe7-9-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They remained there until the late 3rd century BC,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pe9-11_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pe9-11-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while the hinterland was ruled by indigenous monarchs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pe7-9_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pe7-9-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Indigenous Berber monarchs ruled the
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">
        territory
       </a>
       from the 3rd century BC until 40 AD, when it was
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Tingitana" title="Mauretania Tingitana">
        annexed
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       . In the mid-5th century AD, it was overrun by
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       , before being recovered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       in the 6th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       The region was
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Maghreb" title="Muslim conquest of the Maghreb">
        conquered by the Muslims
       </a>
       in the early 8th century AD, but broke away from the
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad Caliphate
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/Berber_Revolt" title="Berber Revolt">
        Berber Revolt
       </a>
       of 740. Half a century later, the Moroccan state was established by the
       <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">
        Idrisid dynasty
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Under the
       <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">
        Almoravid
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">
        Almohad
       </a>
       dynasties,
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       dominated the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Maghreb" title="Greater Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Muslim Spain
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" title="Saadi dynasty">
        Saadi dynasty
       </a>
       ruled the country from 1549 to 1659, followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Alaouite_dynasty" title="Alaouite dynasty">
        Alaouites
       </a>
       from 1667 onwards, who have since been the ruling dynasty of Morocco.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1912, after the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Moroccan_Crisis" title="First Moroccan Crisis">
        First Moroccan Crisis
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Agadir_Crisis" title="Agadir Crisis">
        Agadir Crisis
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fez" title="Treaty of Fez">
        Treaty of Fez
       </a>
       was signed, dividing Morocco into
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Morocco" title="French Morocco">
        French
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" title="Spanish Morocco">
        Spanish protectorates
       </a>
       . In 1956, after 44 years of French rule, Morocco regained independence from
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       , and shortly afterward regained most of the territories under Spanish control.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_Morocco">
        Prehistoric Morocco
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Prehistoric Morocco">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_prehistoric_sites_in_Morocco" title="List of prehistoric sites in Morocco">
        List of prehistoric sites in Morocco
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Archaeological excavations have demonstrated the presence of people in Morocco that were ancestral to
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">
         Homo sapiens
        </a>
       </i>
       , as well as the presence of early human species. The fossilized bones of a 400,000-year-old early human ancestor were discovered in
       <a href="/wiki/Sal%C3%A9" title="Salé">
        Salé
       </a>
       in 1971.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hublin_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hublin-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The bones of several very early
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">
         Homo sapiens
        </a>
       </i>
       were excavated at
       <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Irhoud" title="Jebel Irhoud">
        Jebel Irhoud
       </a>
       in 1991, these were dated using modern techniques in 2017 and found to be at least 300,000 years old, making them the oldest examples of Homo Sapiens discovered anywhere in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2007, small perforated seashell beads were discovered in Taforalt that are 82,000 years old, making them the earliest known evidence of personal adornment found anywhere in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">
        Mesolithic
       </a>
       times, between 20,000 and 5000 years ago, the geography of Morocco resembled a
       <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">
        savanna
       </a>
       more than the present arid landscape.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lubell_1984_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lubell_1984-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While little is known of settlements in Morocco during that period, excavations elsewhere in the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       region have suggested an abundance of game and forests that would have been hospitable to Mesolithic hunters and gatherers, such as those of the
       <a href="/wiki/Capsian_culture" title="Capsian culture">
        Capsian culture
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
        Neolithic
       </a>
       period, which followed the Mesolithic, the savanna was occupied by hunters and herders. The culture of these Neolithic hunters and herders flourished until the region began to desiccate after 5000 BC as a result of climatic changes. The coastal regions of present-day Morocco in the early Neolithic shared in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardium_Pottery" title="Cardium Pottery">
        Cardium Pottery
       </a>
       culture that was common to the entire
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       region. Archaeological excavations have suggested that the
       <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">
        domestication
       </a>
       of cattle and the cultivation of crops both occurred in the region during that period.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">
        Chalcolithic
       </a>
       period, or the copper age, the
       <a href="/wiki/Beaker_culture" title="Beaker culture">
        Beaker culture
       </a>
       reached the north coast of Morocco.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">
        Early history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span id="Carthage_.28c._800_.E2.80.93_c._300_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Carthage_(c._800_–_c._300_BC)">
        Carthage (c. 800 – c. 300 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Carthage (c. 800 – c. 300 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1699" data-file-width="2679" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg/220px-Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg/330px-Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg/440px-Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phenician_plate_with_red_slip_7th_century_BCE_excavated_in_Mogador_island.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
          Phoenician
         </a>
         plate with red
         <a href="/wiki/Slip_(ceramics)" title="Slip (ceramics)">
          slip
         </a>
         , 7th century BCE, excavated on
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mogador_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mogador Island (page does not exist)">
          Mogador Island
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Essaouira" title="Essaouira">
          Essaouira
         </a>
         .
         <a href="/wiki/Sidi_Mohammed_ben_Abdallah_Museum" title="Sidi Mohammed ben Abdallah Museum">
          Sidi Mohammed ben Abdallah Museum
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The arrival of
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenicians
       </a>
       on the Moroccan coast heralded many centuries of rule by foreign powers in the north of Morocco.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Phoenician traders penetrated the western Mediterranean before the 8th century BC, and soon after
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2014)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       set up depots for salt and ore along the coast and up the rivers of the territory of present-day Morocco.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pe5_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pe5-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Major early settlements of the Phoenicians included those at
       <a href="/wiki/Chellah" title="Chellah">
        Chellah
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lixus_(ancient_city)" title="Lixus (ancient city)">
        Lixus
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mogador" title="Mogador">
        Mogador
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mogador is known to have been a Phoenician colony by the early 6th century BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By the 5th century BC,
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">
        the state of Carthage
       </a>
       had extended its hegemony across much of
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">
        Carthage
       </a>
       developed commercial relations with the Berber tribes of the interior, and paid them an annual tribute to ensure their cooperation in the exploitation of raw materials.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Mauretania_.28c._300_BC_.E2.80.93_c._430_AD.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mauretania_(c._300_BC_–_c._430_AD)">
        Mauretania (c. 300 BC – c. 430 AD)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mauretania (c. 300 BC – c. 430 AD)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">
        Mauretania
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Tingitana" title="Mauretania Tingitana">
        Mauretania Tingitana
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1327" data-file-width="2727" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg/220px-Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg/330px-Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg/440px-Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_coins_excavated_in_Essaouira_3rd_century_and_late_Roman_Empire.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
          Roman
         </a>
         coins excavated in Essaouira, 3rd century.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Mauretania was an independent tribal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">
        Berber
       </a>
       kingdom on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       coast of
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        north Africa
       </a>
       , corresponding to northern modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       from about the 3rd century BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burnham_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Burnham-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The earliest known king of Mauretania was
       <a href="/wiki/Bocchus_I" title="Bocchus I">
        Bocchus I
       </a>
       , who ruled from 110 BC to 81 BC. Some of its earliest recorded history relates to
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenician
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">
        Carthaginian
       </a>
       settlements such as Lixus and Chellah.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burnham_17-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Burnham-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Berber kings ruled inland territories overshadowing the coastal outposts of Carthage and
       <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
        Rome
       </a>
       , often as satellites, allowing Roman rule to exist.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       It became a client of the Roman empire in 33 BC, then a full province after Emperor Caligula had the last king,
       <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_of_Mauretania" title="Ptolemy of Mauretania">
        Ptolemy of Mauretania
       </a>
       , executed (AD 40).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rome controlled the vast, ill-defined territory through alliances with the tribes rather than through military occupation, expanding its authority only to those areas, that were economically useful or that could be defended without additional manpower. Hence, Roman administration never extended outside the restricted area of the northern coastal plain and valleys. This strategic region formed part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , governed as
       <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Tingitana" title="Mauretania Tingitana">
        Mauretania Tingitana
       </a>
       , with the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Volubilis" title="Volubilis">
        Volubilis
       </a>
       as its capital.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volubilis01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1212" data-file-width="1926" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Volubilis01.jpg/250px-Volubilis01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Volubilis01.jpg/375px-Volubilis01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Volubilis01.jpg/500px-Volubilis01.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Volubilis01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Roman remains of
         <a href="/wiki/Volubilis" title="Volubilis">
          Volubilis
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the time of the Roman emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
        Augustus
       </a>
       , Mauretania was a vassal state, and its rulers, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Juba_II" title="Juba II">
        Juba II
       </a>
       , controlled all the areas south of Volubilis. But the effective control of Roman legionaries reached as far as the area of Sala Colonia (the castra "Exploratio Ad Mercurios" south of Sala is the southernmost discovered up to now). Some historians believe the Roman frontier reached present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">
        Casablanca
       </a>
       , known then as
       <a href="/wiki/Anfa" title="Anfa">
        Anfa
       </a>
       , which had been settled by the Romans as a port.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lexic_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lexic-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the reign of
       <a href="/wiki/Juba_II" title="Juba II">
        Juba II
       </a>
       , the Augustus founded three
       <a href="/wiki/Colonia_(Roman)" title="Colonia (Roman)">
        colonies
       </a>
       , with Roman citizens, in Mauretania close to the Atlantic coast:
       <a href="/wiki/Iulia_Constantia_Zilil" title="Iulia Constantia Zilil">
        Iulia Constantia Zilil
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iulia_Valentia_Banasa" title="Iulia Valentia Banasa">
        Iulia Valentia Banasa
       </a>
       , and Iulia Campestris Babba. Augustus would eventually found twelve colonies in the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During that period, the area controlled by Rome experienced significant economic development, aided by the construction of
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_roads_in_Morocco" title="Roman roads in Morocco">
        Roman roads
       </a>
       . The area was initially not completely under the control of Rome, and only in the mid-2nd century was a
       <a href="/wiki/Limes" title="Limes">
        limes
       </a>
       built south of Sala extending to Volubilis.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Around 278 AD the Romans moved their regional capital to
       <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">
        Tangier
       </a>
       and Volubilis started to lose importance.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       was introduced to the region in the 2nd century AD, and gained converts in the towns and among slaves as well as among Berber farmers. By the end of the 4th century, the Romanized areas had been Christianized,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title='what is a "romanized" area? (October 2014)'>
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and inroads had been made among the Berber tribes, who sometimes converted en masse.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schism_(religion)" title="Schism (religion)">
        Schismatic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Heresy#Christianity" title="Heresy">
        heretical
       </a>
       movements also developed, usually as forms of political protest. The area had a substantial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
        Jewish
       </a>
       population as well.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Early_Islamic_Morocco_.28c._700_.E2.80.93_c._1060.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Islamic_Morocco_(c._700_–_c._1060)">
        Early Islamic Morocco (c. 700 – c. 1060)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early Islamic Morocco (c. 700 – c. 1060)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="371" data-file-width="636" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG/240px-Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG/360px-Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG/480px-Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG 2x" width="240"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Morocco_and_the_Maghreb_after_the_Berber_Revolt.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Maghreb after the Berber Revolt
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duby_20-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Duby-20">
           [20]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span id="Muslim_conquest_.28c._700.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim_conquest_(c._700)">
        Muslim conquest (c. 700)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Muslim conquest (c. 700)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Maghreb" title="Muslim conquest of the Maghreb">
        Muslim conquest of the Maghreb
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Maghreb" title="Muslim conquest of the Maghreb">
        Muslim conquest of the Maghreb
       </a>
       , that started in the middle of the 7th century AD, was
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Maghreb#Completion_of_the_conquest" title="Muslim conquest of the Maghreb">
        achieved
       </a>
       in the early 8th century. It brought both the Arabic language and
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       to the area. Although part of the larger
       <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">
        Islamic Empire
       </a>
       , Morocco was initially organized as a subsidiary province of
       <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">
        Ifriqiya
       </a>
       , with the local governors appointed by the Muslim governor in
       <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">
        Kairouan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AN33_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AN33-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The indigenous Berber tribes adopted Islam, but retained their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Customary_law" title="Customary law">
        customary laws
       </a>
       . They also paid taxes and tribute to the new Muslim administration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Berber_Revolt_.28740_.E2.80.93_743.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Berber_Revolt_(740_–_743)">
        Berber Revolt (740 – 743)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Berber Revolt (740 – 743)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Berber_Revolt" title="Berber Revolt">
        Berber Revolt
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 740 AD, spurred on by puritanical
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kharijite" title="Kharijite">
        Kharijite
       </a>
       agitators, the native Berber population
       <a href="/wiki/Berber_Revolt" title="Berber Revolt">
        revolted
       </a>
       against the ruling
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ummayad_Caliphate" title="Ummayad Caliphate">
        Ummayad Caliphate
       </a>
       . The rebellion began among the Berber tribes of western Morocco, and spread quickly across the region. Although the insurrection petered out in 742 AD before it reached the gates of
       <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">
        Kairouan
       </a>
       , neither the Umayyad rulers in Damascus nor their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">
        Abbasid
       </a>
       successors managed to re-impose their rule on the areas west of
       <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">
        Ifriqiya
       </a>
       . Morocco passed out of Umayyad and Abbasid control, and fragmented into a collection of small, independent Berber states such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berghwata" title="Berghwata">
        Berghwata
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sijilmassa" title="Sijilmassa">
        Sijilmassa
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Nekor" title="Emirate of Nekor">
        Nekor
       </a>
       , in addition to
       <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">
        Tlemcen
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tahert" title="Tahert">
        Tahert
       </a>
       in what is now western
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duby_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Duby-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Berbers went on to shape their own version of Islam. Some, like the
       <a href="/wiki/Banu_Ifran" title="Banu Ifran">
        Banu Ifran
       </a>
       , retained their connection with radical puritan Islamic sects, while others, like the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berghwata" title="Berghwata">
        Berghwata
       </a>
       , constructed a new
       <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">
        syncretic faith
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AN42_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AN42-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Barghawata_.28744_.E2.80.93_1058.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Barghawata_(744_–_1058)">
        Barghawata (744 – 1058)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Barghawata (744 – 1058)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Barghawata" title="Barghawata">
        Barghawata
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Barghawata" title="Barghawata">
        Barghawatas
       </a>
       were a confederation of Berber groups inhabiting the Atlantic coast of Morocco, who belonged to the
       <a href="/wiki/Masmuda" title="Masmuda">
        Masmuda
       </a>
       Berber tribal division.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duby_20-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Duby-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After allying with the
       <a href="/wiki/Sufri" title="Sufri">
        Sufri
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kharijite" title="Kharijite">
        Kharijite
       </a>
       rebellion in
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       against the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad" title="Umayyad">
        Umayyads
       </a>
       , they established an independent state (CE 744 - 1058) in the area of Tamesna on the Atlantic coast between
       <a href="/wiki/Safi,_Morocco" title="Safi, Morocco">
        Safi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sal%C3%A9" title="Salé">
        Salé
       </a>
       under the leadership of
       <a href="/wiki/Tarif_al-Matghari" title="Tarif al-Matghari">
        Tarif al-Matghari
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Sijilmassa_.28700s_.E2.80.93_1300s.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sijilmassa_(700s_–_1300s)">
        Sijilmassa (700s – 1300s)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sijilmassa (700s – 1300s)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sijilmassa" title="Sijilmassa">
        Sijilmassa
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="512" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg/220px-Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg/330px-Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg/440px-Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trans-Saharan_routes_early.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Berber entrepot
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sijilmassa" title="Sijilmassa">
          Sijilmassa
         </a>
         along the trade routes of the Western Sahara, c. 1000–1500. Goldfields are indicated by light brown shading.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sijilmasa" title="Sijilmasa">
        Sijilmasa
       </a>
       was a medieval Moroccan city and trade
       <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">
        entrepôt
       </a>
       at the northern edge of the Sahara desert. The ruins of the town lie for 8 kilometres (5 mi) along the
       <a href="/wiki/Ziz_River" title="Ziz River">
        River Ziz
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Tafilalt" title="Tafilalt">
        Tafilalt
       </a>
       oasis near the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Rissani" title="Rissani">
        Rissani
       </a>
       . The town's history was marked by several successive invasions by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">
        Berber
       </a>
       dynasties. Up until the 14th century, as the northern terminus for the western
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">
        trans-Sahara trade route
       </a>
       , it was one of the most important trade centres in the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       during the Middle Ages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Kingdom_of_Nekor_.28710_.E2.80.93_1019.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Nekor_(710_–_1019)">
        Kingdom of Nekor (710 – 1019)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Nekor (710 – 1019)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nekor" title="Kingdom of Nekor">
        Kingdom of Nekor
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nekor" title="Kingdom of Nekor">
        Kingdom of Nekor
       </a>
       was an
       <a href="/wiki/Emirate" title="Emirate">
        emirate
       </a>
       centered in the
       <a href="/wiki/Rif" title="Rif">
        Rif
       </a>
       area of Morocco. Its capital was initially located at
       <a href="/wiki/Temsaman_(region)" title="Temsaman (region)">
        Temsaman
       </a>
       , and then moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Nekor" title="Nekor">
        Nekor
       </a>
       . The polity was founded in 710 AD by
       <a href="/wiki/Salih_I_ibn_Mansur" title="Salih I ibn Mansur">
        Salih I ibn Mansur
       </a>
       through a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">
        Caliphate
       </a>
       grant. Under his guidance, the local
       <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">
        Berber
       </a>
       tribes adopted
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       , but later deposed him in favor of one az-Zaydi from the Nafza tribe. They subsequently changed their mind and reappointed Ibn Mansur. His dynasty, the Banū Sālih, thereafter ruled the region until 1019.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 859, the kingdom became subject to a 62 ship-strong group of
       <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">
        Vikings
       </a>
       , who defeated a Moorish force in Nekor that had attempted to interfere with their plunderings in the area. After staying for eight days in Morocco, the Vikings went back to Spain and continued up the east coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Idrisid_dynasty_.28789_.E2.80.93_974.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Idrisid_dynasty_(789_–_974)">
        Idrisid dynasty (789 – 974)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Idrisid dynasty (789 – 974)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">
        Idrisid dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fes_November_2008-42.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Fes_November_2008-42.JPG/220px-Fes_November_2008-42.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Fes_November_2008-42.JPG/330px-Fes_November_2008-42.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Fes_November_2008-42.JPG/440px-Fes_November_2008-42.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fes_November_2008-42.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The school of
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Al_Quaraouiyine" title="University of Al Quaraouiyine">
          Al-Qarawiyyin
         </a>
         in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fes" title="Fes">
          Fes
         </a>
         , established by
         <a href="/wiki/Fatima_al-Fihri" title="Fatima al-Fihri">
          Fatima al-Fihri
         </a>
         during the
         <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">
          Idrisid dynasty
         </a>
         in the 9th century.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">
        Idrisid dynasty
       </a>
       was a Muslim polity centered in Morocco,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which ruled from 788 to 974. Named after the founder
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idriss_I" title="Idriss I">
        Idriss I
       </a>
       , the great grandchild of
       <a href="/wiki/Hasan_ibn_Ali" title="Hasan ibn Ali">
        Hasan ibn Ali
       </a>
       , the Idrisids are believed by some historians to be the founders of the first Moroccan state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Fatimid.2C_Umayyad_and_Zenata_polities_.28c._900_.E2.80.93_c._1060.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fatimid,_Umayyad_and_Zenata_polities_(c._900_–_c._1060)">
        Fatimid, Umayyad and Zenata polities (c. 900 – c. 1060)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fatimid, Umayyad and Zenata polities (c. 900 – c. 1060)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       This equilibrium was upset in the early 900s, when the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid_dynasty" title="Fatimid dynasty">
        Fatimid dynasty
       </a>
       arrived in the Maghreb. Not long after seizing power in
       <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">
        Ifriqiya
       </a>
       , the Fatimids invaded Morocco, conquering both Fez and Sijilmassa. Morocco was fragmented in the aftermath, with Fatimid governors, Idrisid loyalists, new puritan groups and interventionists from Umayyad
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        al-Andalus
       </a>
       all fighting over the region. Opportunistic local governors sold and re-sold their support to the highest bidder. In 965, the Fatimid caliph
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Muizz_Lideenillah" title="Al-Muizz Lideenillah">
        al-Muizz
       </a>
       invaded Morocco one last time and succeeded in establishing some order. Soon after, however, the Fatimids shifted their empire eastward to
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       , with a new capital in
       <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">
        Cairo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Fatimids had assigned the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zirids" title="Zirids">
        Zirids
       </a>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zenaga_people" title="Zenaga people">
        Zenaga
       </a>
       Berber clan centered in Ifriqiya, to watch their western dominions. The Zirids, however, were unable to prevent Morocco from spinning out of their control and crumbling into the hands of a collection of local
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zenata_people" title="Zenata people">
        Zenata
       </a>
       Berber chieftains, most of them clients of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph_of_Cordoba" title="Caliph of Cordoba">
        Caliph of Cordoba
       </a>
       , such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghrawa" title="Maghrawa">
        Maghrawa
       </a>
       in the region of Fez and itinerant rivals, the
       <a href="/wiki/Banu_Ifran" title="Banu Ifran">
        Banu Ifran
       </a>
       to the east.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Berber_dynasties_.28c._1060_.E2.80.93_1549.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Berber_dynasties_(c._1060_–_1549)">
        Berber dynasties (c. 1060 – 1549)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Berber dynasties (c. 1060 – 1549)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg/200px-Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg/300px-Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg/400px-Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rabat_tour_Hassan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Tower" title="Hassan Tower">
          Hassan Tower
         </a>
         , an incomplete minaret in Rabat begun during the Almohad dynasty
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Morocco was at its most powerful under a series of Berber dynasties, which rose to power south of the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">
        Atlas Mountains
       </a>
       and expanded their rule northward, replacing local rulers.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The 11th and 12th centuries witnessed the founding of several significant Berber dynasties led by religious reformers, each dynasty based on a tribal confederation that dominated the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Al-Andalus
       </a>
       for more than 200 years.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Berber dynasties of the (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravids" title="Almoravids">
        Almoravids
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohads" title="Almohads">
        Almohads
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marinid" title="Marinid">
        Marinids
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wattasids" title="Wattasids">
        Wattasids
       </a>
       gave the Berber people some measure of collective identity and political unity under a native regime for the first time in their history.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The dynasties created the idea of an “imperial Maghreb” under Berber aegis, an idea that survived in some form from another.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Almoravid_dynasty_.28c._1060_.E2.80.93_1147.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Almoravid_dynasty_(c._1060_–_1147)">
        Almoravid dynasty (c. 1060 – 1147)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Almoravid dynasty (c. 1060 – 1147)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">
        Almoravid dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">
        Almoravid dynasty
       </a>
       (c.1060-1147) originated among the
       <a href="/wiki/Lamtuna" title="Lamtuna">
        Lamtuna
       </a>
       nomadic
       <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">
        Berber
       </a>
       tribe belonging to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sanhaja" title="Sanhaja">
        Sanhaja
       </a>
       . They succeeded in unifying Morocco after it had been divided among several Zenata principalities in the late 10th century, and annexed the Emirate of Sijilmasa and the Barghawata (Tamesna) into their realm.
      </p>
      <p>
       Under
       <a href="/wiki/Yusuf_ibn_Tashfin" title="Yusuf ibn Tashfin">
        Yusuf ibn Tashfin
       </a>
       , the Almoravids were invited by the Muslim
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">
         taifa
        </a>
       </i>
       princes of
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Al-Andalus
       </a>
       to defend their territories from the Christian kingdoms. Their involvement was crucial in preventing the fall of
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Al-Andalus
       </a>
       . After having succeeded in repelling Christian forces in 1086, Yusuf returned to Iberia in 1090 and annexed most of the major
       <i>
        taifas
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Almoravid power began to decline in the first half of the 12th century, as the dynasty was weakened after its defeat at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">
        battle of Ourique
       </a>
       and because of the agitation of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohads" title="Almohads">
        Almohads
       </a>
       . The conquest of the city of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marrakech" title="Marrakech">
        Marrakech
       </a>
       by the Almohads in 1147 marked the fall of the dynasty. However, fragments of the Almoravids (the
       <a href="/wiki/Banu_Ghaniya" title="Banu Ghaniya">
        Banu Ghaniya
       </a>
       ) continued to struggle in the Balearic Islands and in
       <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
        Tunisia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Almohad_dynasty_.281147_.E2.80.93_1248.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Almohad_dynasty_(1147_–_1248)">
        Almohad dynasty (1147 – 1248)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Almohad dynasty (1147 – 1248)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohad_dynasty" title="Almohad dynasty">
        Almohad dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">
        Almohad Caliphate
       </a>
       was a Moroccan,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Berber
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslim
       </a>
       movement founded in the 12th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brit1_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-brit1-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Almohad movement was started by
       <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Tumart" title="Ibn Tumart">
        Ibn Tumart
       </a>
       among the
       <a href="/wiki/Masmuda" title="Masmuda">
        Masmuda
       </a>
       tribes of southern Morocco. The Almohads first established a Berber state in
       <a href="/wiki/Tinmel" title="Tinmel">
        Tinmel
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">
        Atlas Mountains
       </a>
       in roughly 1120.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brit1_32-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-brit1-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They succeeded in overthrowing the ruling
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravid_Dynasty" title="Almoravid Dynasty">
        Almoravids
       </a>
       in governing Morocco by 1147, when
       <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu'min">
        Abd al-Mu'min al-Gumi
       </a>
       (r. 1130–1163) conquered
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marrakech" title="Marrakech">
        Marrakech
       </a>
       and declared himself Caliph. They then extended their power over all of the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       by 1159.
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Al-Andalus
       </a>
       followed the fate of the Maghreb and all Islamic Iberia was under Almohad rule by 1172.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Marinid_dynasty_.281248_.E2.80.93_1465.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Marinid_dynasty_(1248_–_1465)">
        Marinid dynasty (1248 – 1465)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Marinid dynasty (1248 – 1465)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Marinid_dynasty" title="Marinid dynasty">
        Marinid dynasty
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/1465_Moroccan_revolt" title="1465 Moroccan revolt">
        1465 Moroccan revolt
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chefchaouen,_view_,_Morocco.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="644" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Chefchaouen%2C_view_%2C_Morocco.jpg/220px-Chefchaouen%2C_view_%2C_Morocco.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Chefchaouen%2C_view_%2C_Morocco.jpg/330px-Chefchaouen%2C_view_%2C_Morocco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Chefchaouen%2C_view_%2C_Morocco.jpg/440px-Chefchaouen%2C_view_%2C_Morocco.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chefchaouen,_view_,_Morocco.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Chefchaouen" title="Chefchaouen">
          Chefchaouen
         </a>
         was founded in 1471 by
         <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
          Moorish
         </a>
         exiles from Spain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Marinid_dynasty" title="Marinid dynasty">
        Marinid dynasty
       </a>
       was a
       <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">
        Sunni Muslim
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       dynasty of
       <a href="/wiki/Zenata" title="Zenata">
        Zenata
       </a>
       Berber descent that ruled Morocco from the 13th to the 15th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Britannica-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Marinids overthrew the Almohad dynasty controlling Morocco in 1244,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and briefly controlled all the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       in the mid-14th century. They supported the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Granada" title="Kingdom of Granada">
        Kingdom of Granada
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Al-Andalus
       </a>
       in the 13th and 14th centuries; an attempt to gain a direct foothold on the European side of the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       was however defeated at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_R%C3%ADo_Salado" title="Battle of Río Salado">
        Battle of Río Salado
       </a>
       in 1340 and finished after the
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        Castilian
       </a>
       conquest of
       <a href="/wiki/Algeciras" title="Algeciras">
        Algeciras
       </a>
       from the Marinids in 1344.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Wattasid_dynasty_.281471_.E2.80.93_1549.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wattasid_dynasty_(1471_–_1549)">
        Wattasid dynasty (1471 – 1549)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Wattasid dynasty (1471 – 1549)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Wattasid_dynasty" title="Wattasid dynasty">
        Wattasid dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Wattasid_dynasty" title="Wattasid dynasty">
        Wattasid dynasty
       </a>
       were a ruling dynasty of Morocco. Like the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marinid" title="Marinid">
        Marinids
       </a>
       , they were of
       <a href="/wiki/Zenata" title="Zenata">
        Zenata
       </a>
       Berber descent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bosworth_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bosworth-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The two families were related, and the Marinids recruited many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viziers" title="Viziers">
        viziers
       </a>
       from the Wattasids.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bosworth_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bosworth-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Saadi_dynasty_.281549_.E2.80.93_1659.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Saadi_dynasty_(1549_–_1659)">
        Saadi dynasty (1549 – 1659)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Saadi dynasty (1549 – 1659)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" title="Saadi dynasty">
        Saadi dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG/220px-Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG/330px-Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG/440px-Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kasbahs_in_A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The city of
         <a href="/wiki/A%C3%AFt_Benhaddou" title="Aït Benhaddou">
          Aït Benhaddou
         </a>
         photographed in the evening
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Beginning in 1549, the region was ruled by successive Arab dynasties known as the Sharifian dynasties, who claimed descent from the prophet
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
        Muhammad
       </a>
       . The first of these polities was the
       <a href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" title="Saadi dynasty">
        Saadi dynasty
       </a>
       , which ruled Morocco from 1549 to 1659. From 1509 to 1549, the Saadi rulers had control of only the southern areas. While still recognizing the Wattasids as Sultans until 1528, Saadian's growing power led the Wattasids to attack them and, after an indecisive battle, to recognize their rule over southern Morocco through the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tadla" title="Treaty of Tadla">
        Treaty of Tadla
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bagley_102_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bagley_102-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1659,
       <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_al-Hajj_ibn_Abu_Bakr_al-Dila%27i" title="Mohammed al-Hajj ibn Abu Bakr al-Dila'i">
        Mohammed al-Hajj ibn Abu Bakr al-Dila'i
       </a>
       , the head of the
       <a href="/wiki/Zaouia_of_Dila" title="Zaouia of Dila">
        zaouia of Dila
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was proclaimed sultan of Morocco after the fall of the Saadi dynasty.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EB-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Alaouite_dynasty_.28since_1666.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alaouite_dynasty_(since_1666)">
        Alaouite dynasty (since 1666)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Morocco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Alaouite dynasty (since 1666)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Alaouite_dynasty" title="Alaouite dynasty">
        Alaouite dynasty
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ambassador_Admiral_Abelkader_Perez_1723_1737.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="386" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Ambassador_Admiral_Abelkader_Perez_1723_1737.jpg/220px-Ambassador_Admiral_Abelkader_Perez_1723_1737.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Ambassador_Admiral_Abelkader_Perez_1723_1737.jpg/330px-Ambassador_Admiral_Abelkader_Perez_1723_1737.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Ambassador_Admiral_Abelkader_Perez_1723_1737.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ambassador_Admiral_Abelkader_Perez_1723_1737.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Admiral
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdelkader_Perez" title="Abdelkader Perez">
          Abdelkader Perez
         </a>
         was sent by
         <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Ibn_Sharif" title="Ismail Ibn Sharif">
          Ismail Ibn Sharif
         </a>
         as an ambassador to England in 1723.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Alaouite_dynasty" title="Alaouite dynasty">
        Alaouite dynasty
       </a>
       is the current
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Family_of_Morocco" title="Royal Family of Morocco">
        Moroccan royal family
       </a>
       . The name Alaouite comes from the
       <i>
        ‘Alī
       </i>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Ali" title="Ali">
        ‘Alī ibn Abī Ṭālib
       </a>
       , whose descendant
       <a href="/wiki/Sharif_ibn_Ali" title="Sharif ibn Ali">
        Sharif ibn Ali
       </a>
       became Prince of
       <a href="/wiki/Tafilalt" title="Tafilalt">
        Tafilalt
       </a>
       in 1631. His son
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Rashid_of_Morocco" title="Al-Rashid of Morocco">
        Mulay Al-Rashid
       </a>
       (1664–1672) was able to unite and pacify the country. The Alaouite family claim descent from
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
        Muhammad
       </a>
       through his daughter
       <a href="/wiki/Fatimah" title="Fatimah">
        Fāṭimah az-Zahrah
       </a>
       and her husband
       <a href="/wiki/Ali" title="Ali">
        ‘Alī ibn Abī Ṭālib
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The kingdom was consolidated by
       <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Ibn_Sharif" title="Ismail Ibn Sharif">
        Ismail Ibn Sharif
       </a>
       (1672–1727), who began to create a unified state in the face of opposition from local tribes . Since the Alaouites, in contrast to previous dynasties, did not have the support of a single Berber or
       <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">
        Bedouin
       </a>
       tribe, Isma'īl controlled Morocco through an army of slaves. With these soldiers he drove the
       <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">
        English
       </a>
       from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangiers" title="Tangiers">
        Tangiers
       </a>
       (1684) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spanish
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Larache" title="Larache">
        Larache
       </a>
       in 1689. The unity of Morocco did not survive his death — in the ensuing power struggles the tribes became a political and military force once again, and it was only with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohammed_III_of_Morocco" title="Mohammed III of Morocco">
        Muhammad III
       </a>
       (1757–1790) that the kingdom was unified again.The idea of centralization was abandoned and the tribes allowed to preserve their autonomy.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       On 20 December 1777,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Morocco became one of the first states to recognize the sovereignty of a newly independent
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the reigns of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohammed_IV_of_Morocco" title="Mohammed IV of Morocco">
        Muhammad IV
       </a>
       (1859–1873) and
       <a href="/wiki/Hassan_I_of_Morocco" title="Hassan I of Morocco">
        Hassan I
       </a>
       (1873–1894), the Alaouites tried to foster trade links, especially with European countries and the United States. The army and administration were also modernized to consolidate control over the Berber and Bedouin tribes. In 1859, Morocco went to war with Spain. The independence of Morocco was guaranteed at the Conference of Madrid in 1880,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with France also gaining significant influence over Morocco. Germany attempted to counter the growing French influence, leading to the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Moroccan_Crisis" title="First Moroccan Crisis">
        First Moroccan Crisis
       </a>
       of 1905–1906, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Moroccan_Crisis" title="Second Moroccan Crisis">
        Second Moroccan Crisis
       </a>
       of 1911. Morocco became a French
       <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">
        Protectorate
       </a>
       through the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fez" title="Treaty of Fez">
        Treaty of Fez
       </a>
       in 1912.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="European_influence_.28c._1830_.E2.80.93_1956.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_influence_(c._1830_–_1956)">
        European influence (c. 1830 – 1956)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
